## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics / constitutive modeling of thermo-mechanical stress–strain behavior)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is a classic setup for constitutive laws in mechanics of materials (elasticity, plasticity, viscoplasticity) with temperature-dependent stiffness, yield/flow stress, and thermal softening/expansion effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (polynomial): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (nonlinear stiffness–temperature trend)
- Thermoelastic strain offset (effective strain): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T + c2)) (stress reduced by thermal expansion-like term; c2 acts as reference-temperature shift)
- Hyperelastic (neo-Hookean-type in uniaxial form): sigma = c0 * ((1 + epsilon) - 1 / (1 + epsilon)**2) (finite-strain elastic response)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit or rearranged explicit fit form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (elastic + nonlinear strain hardening; often inverted numerically for sigma(epsilon))
- Hollomon power-law hardening with thermal softening factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (plastic flow curve with multiplicative temperature effect)
- Ludwik-type hardening (strain offset): sigma = c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (yield/offset plus power-law hardening)
- Swift hardening with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (strain hardening with temperature-dependent strength coefficient)
- Voce hardening (saturating flow stress): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (plastic flow approaching saturation stress)
- Voce + temperature softening: sigma = c0 + (c1 * exp(c2 * T)) * (1 - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (saturation and rate of hardening modulated by T)
- Zerilli–Armstrong-like structure without strain-rate term: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 + c3 * exp(c4 * T) (sum of athermal hardening and thermally activated softening/hardening term)
- Logarithmic hardening (empirical metals/polymer fits): sigma = c0 + c1 * log(c2 * epsilon + 1) + c3 * T (slow hardening with possible linear temperature drift)
- Bilinear elastic–plastic surrogate (smooth transition): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon - c2 * log(c3 * epsilon + 1) (captures initial linear rise then reduced slope/softening post-yield in a smooth way)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elasticity → sigma proportional to epsilon; temperature enters primarily by scaling the slope (effective modulus).
- Thermal expansion/stress-free strain shift → sigma depends on (epsilon - c * (T + c0)), i.e., temperature acts like an offset in strain.
- Plastic hardening at moderate strains → power laws in epsilon (epsilon**n) are common; n controls curvature (concave/convex hardening).
- Saturation of flow stress at large strain → exponential approach-to-limit forms like (1 - exp(-c * epsilon)) to represent Voce-type saturation.
- Thermal softening of strength/modulus → multiplicative exp(c * T) or polynomial-in-T prefactors on elastic/plastic terms (often decreasing with T depending on sign).
- Additive decomposition of mechanisms → sigma as a sum of an athermal term (depends on epsilon) plus a thermal term (depends on T) is common in physically-motivated fits.
- Finite-strain effects → rational forms in (1 + epsilon) (e.g., (1+epsilon) - 1/(1+epsilon)^2) appear when converting from stretch-based hyperelasticity to engineering strain.
- Slow hardening / near-log behavior → log(c * epsilon + 1) captures diminishing returns of stress increase with strain in some regimes.
- Yield-like intercept behavior → additive constants (c0) represent initial yield/flow stress before hardening contributions grow with epsilon.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$-c_0(T - c_1) + \epsilon^{c_2} \cdot c_3 \cdot (T - c_4)$$

With c1 = c4 = 352.1579..., so:
$$(-c_0 + c_3 \cdot \epsilon^{c_2})(T - c_1)$$

Expanding:
$$T(-c_0 + c_3 \epsilon^{c_2}) + c_1 c_0 - c_1 c_3 \epsilon^{c_2}$$

So GT = $T \cdot c_3 \epsilon^{c_2} - c_0 T + c_0 c_1 - c_1 c_3 \epsilon^{c_2}$

The key structure is: **linear in T**, with the T-coefficient being $(-c_0 + c_3 \epsilon^{c_2})$, and the constant term being $c_1(c_0 - c_3 \epsilon^{c_2})$.

Note: The T-independent part is exactly $-c_1$ times the T-coefficient. This means GT = $(T - c_1)(-c_0 + c_3 \epsilon^{c_2})$.

So the essential form is:
$$\alpha T + \beta \epsilon^{\gamma} T + \delta + \zeta \epsilon^{\gamma}$$

where $\delta = -\alpha c_1$ and $\zeta = -\beta c_1$ (the constant and epsilon^gamma terms are NOT independent of the T-coefficient terms).

Let me check which candidates can produce this structure.

For a candidate to match, it needs:
1. A term linear in T (constant coefficient): $\alpha T$
2. A term $T \cdot \epsilon^{\gamma}$ — this is the critical cross-term
3. A constant term
4. A term $\epsilon^{\gamma}$

The cross-term $T \cdot \epsilon^{c_2}$ is crucial. Most candidates don't have this.

Let me scan for candidates that can produce $T \cdot \epsilon^{c_2}$:

**Candidates with potential T·ε interaction:**
- Candidate 1: $T \cdot c_1/(c_2 \epsilon + c_3)$ — this is $T/(a\epsilon+b)$, not $T\epsilon^{0.626}$
- Candidate 2: Similar rational function
- Candidate 10: $c_6 \epsilon (T+c_7)^{c_8}$ — if c8=1, gives $c_6\epsilon(T+c_7) = c_6\epsilon T + c_6 c_7 \epsilon$. But we need $T\epsilon^{0.626}$, not $T\epsilon^1$.
- Candidate 11: Same issue with $\epsilon(T+c_7)^{c_8}$
- Candidate 12: $T \cdot c_0 (c_1+\epsilon)^{c_2}$ — this gives $T(c_1+\epsilon)^{c_2}$, which is NOT $T\epsilon^{c_2}$ unless $c_1=0$. If c1=0, this becomes $T\epsilon^{c_2}$! Then the full expression: $T c_0 \epsilon^{c_2} + c_3\epsilon^{c_4} + c_5 + c_6\epsilon^{c_7} + c_8\epsilon$. We need: $\alpha T + \beta T\epsilon^{\gamma} + \delta + \zeta\epsilon^{\gamma}$. Setting c1=0: $T c_0 \epsilon^{c_2}$ provides $\beta T\epsilon^{\gamma}$. But we also need $\alpha T$ (plain T term), which is missing! No standalone T term.
- Candidate 13: $T c_0 + T c_1(c_2+\epsilon)^{c_3}$ — if c2=0: $T c_0 + T c_1 \epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon^{c_5} + c_6 + c_7\epsilon^{c_8} + c_9\epsilon$. This gives $T(c_0 + c_1\epsilon^{c_3})$ plus epsilon terms and constant. This CAN match! Set c3=0.626, combine epsilon power terms, set c_9=0 or absorb. We need: constant = $c_0 c_1$-related constraint, but constants are free. Yes, this matches structurally: $T c_0 + T c_1 \epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon^{c_5} + c_6 + c_7\epsilon^{c_8} + c_9\epsilon$. Set c_5=c_3=0.626, c_9=0, c_7=0 or c_8 arbitrary with c_7=0. Then: $T c_0 + T c_1 \epsilon^{0.626} + c_4\epsilon^{0.626} + c_6$. This matches!

- Candidate 39: $c_5\epsilon(T+c_6)^{c_7}$ — if c7=1: $c_5\epsilon T + c_5 c_6\epsilon$. Need $T\epsilon^{0.626}$, not $T\epsilon$.
- Candidate 40: Same issue.

- Candidate 26: $c_5\epsilon/(Tc_6+c_7) + c_8/(Tc_6+c_7)$ — rational in T, not polynomial.

Let me now carefully verify Candidate 13:

**Candidate 13:** $T c_0 + T c_1(c_2+\epsilon)^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon^{c_5} + c_6 + c_7\epsilon^{c_8} + c_9\epsilon$

Set c_2=0: $T c_0 + T c_1 \epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon^{c_5} + c_6 + c_7\epsilon^{c_8} + c_9\epsilon$

GT = $-c_0^{GT} T + c_3^{GT}\epsilon^{c_2^{GT}} T + c_0^{GT}c_1^{GT} - c_1^{GT}c_3^{GT}\epsilon^{c_2^{GT}}$

Match: $c_0 = -0.5449$, $c_1\epsilon^{c_3} = 1.518\epsilon^{0.626}$ so $c_1=1.518, c_3=0.626$.
$c_4\epsilon^{c_5}$: set to $-c_1^{GT}c_3^{GT}\epsilon^{c_2^{GT}} = -352.16 \times 1.518 \epsilon^{0.626}$, so $c_4 = -534.8, c_5=0.626$.
$c_6 = c_0^{GT}c_1^{GT} = 0.5449 \times 352.16 = 191.9$.
Set $c_7=0, c_9=0$.

This works! ✓

Now let me check all other candidates systematically for the $T\epsilon^{c_2}$ cross-term:

Most candidates have terms like $T c_0 + c_1\epsilon^{c_2} + ...$ with NO T·ε cross-term. These cannot match because the GT requires a $T\epsilon^{0.626}$ term, and without it, you can't produce the correct dependence.

Let me verify candidates that might have the cross-term:

**Candidate 1:** $T c_0 + T c_1/(c_2\epsilon+c_3) + ...$. The $T/(a\epsilon+b)$ term is NOT equivalent to $T\epsilon^{0.626}$ for any constants.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** Similar rational structure. Cannot produce $T\epsilon^{0.626}$.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** $T c_0 + c_1\epsilon^{c_2} + c_3\sin(Tc_4+c_5) + ...$. Has sin(T) not $T\epsilon^{c}$. Set c_3=0 to kill sin, but then no T·ε cross-term.
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** $T c_0 + c_1\epsilon^{c_2} + c_3 + c_4\epsilon^{c_5} + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon$. No T·ε cross-term.
Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** $T c_0 + T c_1 + c_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4 + c_5\epsilon^{c_6} + c_7\epsilon$. $T(c_0+c_1)$ is just $\alpha T$. No T·ε cross-term.
Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** $T^{c_0} c_1 + ...$. If c_0=1, just $c_1 T$. No T·ε cross-term.
Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** $T c_0 + c_1\epsilon^{c_2} + c_3\epsilon^{c_4} + c_5 + c_6\epsilon^{c_7}$. No T·ε cross-term.
Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** $T c_0 + c_1\epsilon^{c_2} + c_3 + c_4\epsilon^{c_5} + c_6\epsilon$. No T·ε cross-term.
Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 9:** $T c_0/(Tc_1+c_2) + ...$. Rational in T. If c_1=0: $Tc_0/c_2 + ... + c_8/c_2$. Just $\alpha T + const$. No T·ε cross-term.
Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** $... + c_6\epsilon(T+c_7)^{c_8} + c_9\epsilon$. If c_8=1: $c_6\epsilon T + c_6 c_7\epsilon + c_9\epsilon$. This gives $T\epsilon$, not $T\epsilon^{0.626}$. For general c_8, $(T+c_7)^{c_8}$ is a power of T, not ε. So this gives $\epsilon \cdot f(T)$, not $T \cdot \epsilon^{c}$. Cannot match.
Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 11:** Same issue as 10. $c_6\epsilon(T+c_7)^{c_8}$ — this is $\epsilon^1 \cdot g(T)$, not $T\epsilon^{0.626}$.
Candidate 11 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 12:** $T c_0(c_1+\epsilon)^{c_2} + c_3\epsilon^{c_4} + c_5 + c_6\epsilon^{c_7} + c_8\epsilon$

If c_1=0: $T c_0 \epsilon^{c_2} + c_3\epsilon^{c_4} + c_5 + c_6\epsilon^{c_7} + c_8\epsilon$

We need $\alpha T + \beta T\epsilon^{0.626} + \delta + \zeta\epsilon^{0.626}$.

This gives $T c_0\epsilon^{c_2}$ but NO standalone $\alpha T$ term. We'd need $c_0\epsilon^{c_2}$ to sometimes equal a constant (for the $\alpha T$ part), which is impossible since ε varies.

Unless... we think of it differently. Can we set c_2=0? Then $T c_0(c_1+\epsilon)^0 = T c_0$. But then we lose the $T\epsilon^{0.626}$ term.

We can't get both $T$ and $T\epsilon^{0.626}$ from a single $T(c_1+\epsilon)^{c_2}$ term. Actually, $(c_1+\epsilon)^{c_2}$ with c_1≠0 is NOT $\alpha + \beta\epsilon^{c_2}$ in general. So this doesn't work.
Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 13:** Already verified above. ✓
Candidate 13 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 14-51:** Let me check each for T·ε cross-terms.

**Candidates 14-25, 27-38, 41-51:** These all have structures like $Tc_0 + f(\epsilon) + g(...)$ or no T dependence at all, or T through log/exp/sin/rational functions. None have a $T\epsilon^c$ cross-term.

Let me double-check a few:

**Candidate 21:** $Tc_0 + T^{c_1}c_2 + ...$. If c_1=1: $(c_0+c_2)T$. No cross-term.
Candidate 21 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 26:** $... + c_5\epsilon/(Tc_6+c_7) + c_8/(Tc_6+c_7) + ...$. If c_6=0: just constants. No T·ε cross-term.
Candidate 26 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 39:** $c_5\epsilon(T+c_6)^{c_7}$. This is $\epsilon^1 \cdot (T+c_6)^{c_7}$, not $T\epsilon^{c}$ with fractional ε power.
Candidate 39 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 40:** Same as 39 issue.
Candidate 40 verdict: [NO MATCH]
